--- Commit Message ---
LU-12273 lod: metadata overstriping

This adds overstriping for MDTs, similar to overstriping
for OSTs (added in LU-9846).  This adds a new option to
setdirstripe, -C, allowing creation of more than one stripe
per MDT.  It is also possible to place multiple stripes on
the same MDT using specific striping with -m.

This allows a single directory to more fully use the full
capability of each MDT in the file system.

Two limitations of note:
1. This requires > 1 MDT, otherwise the DNE subsystem is
not initialized.
2. Due to recovery limitations, we allow a max of only 5
stripes per MDT.

MDT overstriping increases mdtest-hard-write performance by
up to 13%, mdtest-hard-stat by 93%, at the cost of a slight
drop in mdtest-hard-read (7%), with no change in delete.

4 MDTs, 1 stripe/MDT:
mdtest-hard-write      117.399467 kIOPS : time 339.496 seconds
mdtest-hard-stat      727.020749 kIOPS : time 55.666 seconds
mdtest-hard-read      245.556392 kIOPS : time 162.897 seconds
mdtest-hard-delete      104.379111 kIOPS : time 382.710 seconds

4 MDTs, 4 stripes/MDTs:
mdtest-hard-write      132.963290 kIOPS : time 309.093 seconds
mdtest-hard-stat     1408.161148 kIOPS : time 30.107 seconds
mdtest-hard-read      229.383910 kIOPS : time 179.576 seconds
mdtest-hard-delete      103.284369 kIOPS : time 398.442 seconds

Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity env=ONLY=300u serverversion=2.14.0

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-01-23 20:11:57.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

So this is interesting - here's the results of attempting to create an a 4 stripe overstriped directory (server has 2 MDTs) from a client which supports it (master + patch) to a server which does not (ES6):
"[root@cent801 lustre]# lfs setdirstripe -C 4 newdir
[root@cent801 lustre]# lfs getdirstripe newdir
lmv_stripe_count: 2 lmv_stripe_offset: 0 lmv_hash_type: crush,overstriped
mdtidx           FID[seq:oid:ver]
     0           [0x200000400:0x2:0x0]
     1           [0x240000401:0x2:0x0]
"

So it created the maximum number of stripes, 1 for each MDT, which is a reasonable response. 
 The part that troubles me is the overstriped flag appearing in the hash type.  It's not a huge problem, but it is misleading.

Thoughts on that?  Should the client strip it, and if so, how would it decide to strip it?  Normally I would make that the job of the server but obviously that can't be done here since we're talking about interop with an older server.  (On new servers, the overstriping flag is stripped if for some reason we don't actually overstripe.  (generally because # of stripes requested is < number of available MDTs, so overstriping isn't needed))

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-01-23 20:16:15.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

If we added a connect flag, we could have new clients strip the overstriping flag when talking to old servers.  Otherwise I don't see how we could easily do it without adding a "check for the actual number of stripes created" step on the client side, which seems like a big pain.  (Performance cost probably a non-issue since it would be a local query and remote directory creation already isn't cheap.  But it still seems like a pain.)

So we could add a connect flag, the purpose of which would be to strip the overstriping flag from requests when the server didn't support it.  That would be the only thing it did, but that doesn't seem *crazy* to me.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-01-24 16:41:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10:

AFAICS, the server will already strip flags not in LMV_HAS_FLAG_SUPPORTED. At that point, I'm not sure whether it will reject the mkdir as having too many stripes (or duplicate MDT indices for a specific layout), or if it would just proceed with a reduced (non-overstriped) mkdir?

That is why I asked about moving the MDS version check further down the sanity test - so that basic "new client mkdir with overstripe" can be tested against an old MDS in autotest with "Test-Parameters: serverversion=2.12" and "...2.14".

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-01-24 16:52:34.000000000) ---
Patch Set 10: -Code-Review

Sorry, I read your emails out of order, and now see that you did the manual interop test already. I'd still like the sanity test to do some basic interop test, just to confirm that it doesn't cause the client or server to crash or create a corrupted directory (returning an error would be acceptable, but the current behavior of creating a directory with fewer stripes is better).

Leaving the overstripe flag set is not ideal, but unlikely to be high on anyone's priority list of problems, IMHO. I don't think the presence of this flag in an existing directory is really used for anything?  Older clients would print "unknown_0100" with getdirstripe, but AFAIK there is no other fallout?

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2023-01-30 20:59:48.000000000) ---
Patch Set 11:

So, I need some help from someone who understands RS_MAX_LOCKS.  (Andreas, Lai...?)

It's documented best where it's used in mdt_link_parents_lock, and then in
test 230r and test 300uf (a copy of 230r with MDT overstriping).

The RS_MAX_LOCKS limitation was used (by me, it seems) to decide the limit
of stripes per MDT was 5.

Basically, that's not really correct.  When migrating from an overstriped
directory with various links in place, we end up using as many as 12 locks.

But I can't figure out how we arrive there, or how RS_MAX_LOCKS is affected
by MDT count or stripes_per_mdt.

If there are more than 2 MDTs with 5 stripes per MDT, it seems like we use
*up to* 12 locks in the migration.  But it's the same if there are 3 MDTs,
4 MDTs, or 8 MDTs - The number of locks rises, but then doesn't scale with
the number of MDTs.

It also doesn't seem to scale with the number of stripes per MDT - I tried
reducing and increasing that value (though not very high, I could play with
it more) and it didn't seem to affect the number of locks required.

In short:
What on earth?  I don't understand DNE enough to figure out if there is
truly a dependence on the number of MDTs (which would be tricky to deal with)
or stripes per MDT.  Like I said, it doesn't seem to get past a certain number
of locks (12), even if I up the # of MDTs and stripes per MDT.

Lai, Andreas, (or anyone else),

Do you have insight on this?  Specifically, how many locks are expected to be
used in the RS_MAX_LOCKS context with metadata overstriping?  What does it
depend on?

Is there a possibility that I'm not hitting the lock max because some
operations are completing quickly?

This is the last significant thing remaining to finalize this.  (There are a
few tests and minor bugs and style stuff, but this is the only major thing.)
